  1. I switched to a foil razor from a blade about 4 years ago due to persistent and painful ingrown hairs. Additionally my hair is thick and grows rather quickly so regular blade shaving had to be eliminated. After much research at that time, I went for a Braun Series 7 and was fairly loyal to it until recently. My loyalty to the foil razor even persisted through the last couple years of loathing shaving due to irritation and areas that were not always shaved properly i.e. neck and jaw line. I tried pre-shave gels and creams before finally doing research for a new shaver. Various site rankings and products reviewed led me to considering the Norelco 3D line and long story short, I made the purchase with moderate expectations despite some of the glowing reviews.<br /><br />I tried it last night initially, expecting the first time to be a bit uncomfortable, as the skin and hair will typically take 3 weeks to adapt to a new method of shaving. However, the shave was absolutely amazing. From the relatively quiet noise to the fact that hairs were not being spit out all over my counter, were already a huge improvement over the Series 7. However the shave itself was amazingly proficient and comfortable. It was as if the razor molded to every contour and edge of my jaw line; the upper lip area (which typically was the most uncomfortable spot to shave) was a breeze and just took one pass as opposed to 2 or 3. The neck did feel slightly irritated, but I believe that's because my hair was actually shaved and trimmed for the first time as I usually had to resort to a blade to get all the missed areas with the foil.<br /><br />If you have been on the fence; are prone to ingrown hairs; or have frequent irritation after shaving with a foil or blade, I highly recommend this product. I did choose the version with the Jet Clean system mainly to do \\"a maintenance clean\\" about every 3 weeks or so as I plan to rinse and manually clean the majority of the time.

  16. This review is for the Norelco Philips Sensotouch 3D 1280x. I bought this razor from Costco in Asia. It includes the shaver, travel bag, one small (tiny) brush, a triangular recharge stand, the cutter cover, and a plug. All this in an oversized box. Looks like you're getting alot, but it's all boxed space. Been using this for 3 weeks now. I have to say, this shaver is over-rated. I've read hundreds of reviews for shavers before I decided on this one. And it's only because I saw it in Costco. The shaver sound is very much quieter. But I think that's because the shaver is weaker and slower than the Braun. I shaver is nice to hold, but that can be said for the Braun. The digital 'time left' viewer is nice, but it's not like it's necessary for a good shave. The shave, to get the point, does not cut as well as the Braun. I find myself shaving for longer periods because I don't feel it has gotten all the hairs on my chin and neck. It feels weak and it doesn't give me the confidence that I can leave the house with a thorough shave. In fact, to me, the shave feels girly. Additional comments: (1) True, you cannot charge directly from the chord. You MUST have the triangular stand to charge. I travel often and this is not conevenient. (2) You must unplug the stand after use or else the stand will have a shorter life span. It's a hassle to plug in and then plug out. Poor engineering. (3) The brush is tiny. Sure, it's nice to use on the blades, but chances are it'll get lost before 30 days. (4) Small, if not tiny, trimmer. I guess if you have thin sideburns, but I'm not sure why they're saving space with a tiny trimmer. Pros: (1) Waterproof. Can use in the shower. (2) Wash with water. Sure this can save money in not buying cleaners and disinfectants. But I'd rather use alcohol to clean my blades since it's got a lot of bacteria after so many uses. (3) Cheaper than a Braun. But in retrospect, I may want to shell out an additional $100-200 for a Braun. I'm sure many people will say it's buyer's remorse, but after much research, I thought I was getting a good shaver. But after use for 3 weeks, I think I got a mediocre product which I'll use, but after getting my money's worth, be looking forward to buying another shaver.

For sideburns, this shaver has a pop-out cutter that does a good job - but it still leaves too much stubble and the round rotary head can't get close enough... making a clean line difficult. Since my initial experience, I've shaved two more times (both dry). The shaver is doing great on my cheeks, but is still irritating my neck. The razor itself is easier to hold and use, and is much lighter and quieter than the Braun.<br /><br />As other reviewers have mentioned the razor has to be charged in either the stand or the cleaning unit. What I do have a problem with is the fact that the razor has to be removed from the charging unit as soon as the charge is complete. It cannot remain in the charging stand or cleaning unit when fully charged or it will damage the battery. In my opinion the poorest design of this razor.<br /><br />The cleaning unit is ok, nothing special. I think that Braun's design is much better in this aspect. Even though the Braun refill cartridges are more expensive than the Norelco's, I like the fact that it is much neater and eaiser to use. When the cartridge is no longer useable you just cap it and throw it away, No having to clean the unit and possibly spilling cleaning solution when it is time to replenish the supply with the Norelco. Also the Braun's cleaning unit heat dries the razor. The Norelco just air dries in the unit.<br /><br />Overall I am happy with this product. I will continue to use it and prefer it to the Braun.h neater and eaiser to use. When the cartridge is no longer useable you just cap it and throw it away, No having to clean the unit and possibly spilling cleaning solution when it is time to replenish the supply with the Norelco. My only complaints: Non-Universal Power Supply - I also own the Philips Body Shaver and while the power cords look the same and actually do plug into the charging bases, they are not compatible. I found this out when I plugged the wrong one into this unit and all of the lights started flashing at the same time with an alarm beep. Nothing in the instructions warned of this problem and I had to figure it out on my own. Silly because if I was travelling for extended time I would have to pack both cords which look identical. FAIL by Philips. Head Design - While the head is designed very well in order to get into tight places on the face, the design for opening the heads for cleaning is annoying. Each head is hinged on the outside and individually and since they recommend cleaning after each shave, you have to grab each head and open individually. Also I have had a couple of times when my chin caught one of the heads and popped it open. This has only happened twice and I have learned how to use it without this happening. Cleaning Unit - I have no plans of using this unit as I am not a fan of the scent of the cleaning solution. Reminds me of the chemical smell of a freshly cleaned public bathroom. Just opening the heads and blowing them out into my shower after each shave does the trick and the water simply carries all the hair down the drain.

I contacted Norelco and they sent a replacement handle. I was also told that I should fully discharge before recharging because of a presumed memory effect (which I did not believe was supposed to be an issue with Li-ion batteries); that made no difference. Roughly the same thing happened with the second handle. Phoning Phillips again, I was told this time that the amount of energy used depended on shaving conditions and that the cutters required more force to move through shaving cream. Up to then I had been using wet shave with a container of brush-applied shaving cream -- which was quite viscous. After the cream ran out, I switched to the same brand of shaving soap -- which is less viscous. Turns out that the battery capacity rose after 1-2 cycles to 41-42 min, which is where it is now. Other than that I am very happy with the shaves -- much closer that my 10+ year-old Norelco with which I had dry-shaved until the head broke. So . . . be prepared for the capacity to &#34;adjust&#34; to your shaving conditions, which will probably mean that you will NOT get a full 60 min of shaving time. If you can deal with that, it's a very nice unit to use. And realize that not all of the service techs at Norelcto will provide useful answers.

  183. First some background on me: I have what I consider to be a moderate beard - the only possible exception being the chin area which is hard to shave with either an electric or a razor. In the past I have used electric shavers mostly - the most recent before this new Norelco being a Norelco 7825XL which I purchased in 2004. When I needed a really close shave, I would use my multi-blade razor. Over Christmas I decided to finally treat myself and upgrade to the 1280X with the cleaning system. Plus my brother had the 1280X and recommended it highly to me and his beard is heavier than mine. My thinking on getting the cleaning system was that I wanted some mechanism to clean out the skin oil in addition to the shavings. Running the heads under the water after each shave (as I do) gets rid of the shavings, but I don't think it flushes out all the skin oil. Overall conclusion: this electric razor is: (a) the best electric I have ever used, and (b) routinely gives me as close a shave as my razor without the mess and in considerably less time. The test I use in judging a shaver is how much time has to elapse after the shave to get to the point that when I feel my face, it is clear to me that I need to shave. With a razor I can easily go 24 hours before I begin to even think about shaving again. With the old Norelco shaver, 24 hours was the maximum that I could comfortably go in between shavings. And if it was date night, I would almost always shave again to remove the growth that had occurred since my morning shave. The 1280X easily lets me go 24 hours in between shaves. More about the shaver: Since my old Norelco was a 2004 vintage, I was not terribly surprised that progress had been made in shaver design in the intervening 7 years. There are 3 big differences: 1. the shaver head which contains the 3 rotary blade assemblies \\"floats\\" which allows the individual shaver heads to adjust to the contour of my face and clearly is part of the reason I get a better shave. If you look closely at the head assembly you will notice that (a) the entire assembly flexes, and (b) the individual razor assembly can also flex apart from the larger head assembly. Seems like a much improved design to me. 2. I do not have to push down as hard as I did with the old Norelco to get a proper shave. And except for the most difficult chin areas, I do not have go back and forth multiple times in order to get a good close shave there. 3. Less of a big deal to me but still noticeable - the noise made by the razor is considerably less than my old Norelco. Disclosure: the shaver is designed to be used in the shower and/or with shaving creme. I have not tried that since the dry shaving that I do gives me such great results. The 1280X has a digital read-out on the body of the shaver telling you how many minutes of charge are remaining on the shaver's rechargeable battery. I have had the 1280X for about a month and a half and for me I am averaging about 2 minutes of battery usage per shave. When the read-out got down to 4 minutes remaining (after about a month), I got the cleaner system out and did my first cleaning on the shaver. Turns out it charges the shaver while it is doing the cleaning. Back to the Jet Clean system - you start of by filling the bowl which is housed in the lower portion of the cleaning assembly with the cleaning solution provided. Plug in the cleaning system, insert the 1280X shaver head down, and turn it on and walk away. I had expected the cleaning solution to contain either alcohol or acetone, but not so according to the ingredients listed on the bottle. Whatever is in the solution it did a great job of cleaning including the skin oil that inevitably gets into the shaver heads. A hour or so later, the shaver was clean, dry and fully charged. I then emptied out the solution into a travel bottle I had to hold the solution for re-use next month when I would repeat the entire process. As I was transferringthe solution out of the cleaning system I purposely did not transfer the \\"dregs\\" if you will at the bottom of the bowl because there was clearly visible particulate matter in the solution. No surprise there. The solution is inexpensive and available on Amazon. Traveling with the 1280X - From my experience so far I think I could travel with the 1280X for 25 days without needing to take the charging stand and cord with me - that's assuming it was fully charged when I left (60 minutes of shaving time is the maximum charge). If I was going to be traveling for 30 days or more - then no question those items would have to come with me. If I could ask the engineers for one enhancement it would be the trimmer. I actually like the trimmer on the old 7825XL better. Why ? Well it extends out further from the body of the shaver and the trimmer is simply bigger. I primarily use the trimmer for the pesky ear hair and while the trimmer on the 1280X does an OK job, the old trimmer was better. Conclusion: Highly recommended without reservation for all except for those few guys who have an exceptionally heavy beard. For those guys I would recommend at least checking the 1280X out if that is at all possible.

  237. Let me set the background for you: I have been shaving over half a century now. Long ago I became convinced triple-header IS the way to go, and for many years I felt that Norelco produces excellent razors. I believe this review is without prejudice, but I wanted all of the cards out on the table. In addition, besides shaving my face, less the area around my goatee, I also shave the sides and back of my head where the remnants of my scalp attempt, pitiably, to grow<br />.<br />First of all, this product is not just a razor, it is a shaving system. Not only to you get a razor, but it also comes with a device that deep cleans the shaving heads.<br /><br />About the razor:<br />1. It contains its own battery, so you are not chained to an outlet while you shave. Potentially useful, if not necessary.<br />2. The battery will last a month, easy. It shows the charge on a display in the handle, which measures the strength of the battery in remaining minutes, with a cap at 60. Given that my shaving, both face and head, takes less than 2 minutes, there is no issue if you want to use it that long without recharging. And I suspect it will go longer than 60 minutes total.<br />3. I used to be that in order to clean your razor, you had to:<br /> a. Remove the head<br /> b. Remove the bracket that head the razor nodules in<br /> c. Take the actual razors out of the protective shield that runs across your skin, and clean each piece separately<br /><br />Now all you have to do is flip up each individual node and brush off the heads and catch basin. After that I rinse it under the water to flush out anything I may have missed. This I do on a daily basis. I then leave the shaving module open, to dry during the day.<br /><br />About the cleaning system:<br />Once every week or so, I will, after doing the daily cleaning, which takes about 30 seconds, place the razor in the cleaning device, after having filled that with the cleaning solution. I then turn on the cleaning system and it will periodically dunk the heads into the solution and turn the razor on and off several times while the heads are submerged. It then brings the heads out of the solution, lets the solution drip off, then repeat the process. I walk away once I get it started because it will do it for some time and it can take care of itself – it doesn’t need us humans.<br /><br />The shave is incredible. My skin is smooth after my shave.<br /><br />The only con I have about this system is the price. I’ve never before spent even $100 for a razor, this one, on sale, was over $200. However, the adage “You get what you pay for” comes true in a very positive way. Under the presumption that this system will last many years, it should still be very worthwhile acquisition. The manufacturer recommends that the head assembly be replaced every year, and I’m sure that that will cost a few dollars.<br /><br />Overall I have nothing but praise for the system. I will update the post in a year to let you know how it is performing.

  260. This shaver was purchased as a replacement for my Braun 7 series. I have not tried the wet shave, which other reviewers report is even better than the dry shave, but the dry shave for me was very good. This is an expensive product and there are a couple of annoying areas which Philips really should have thought about. The major down side is that the shaver should not be left plugged in to the mains once the battery is charged. This is very inconvenient particularly if you use the jet clean system. It is very irritating to have to take the shaver out of the jet clean system once it has finished cleaning or charging. The clean cycle takes quite some time. Users are unlikely to be waiting around for the cleaning process to finish so that they are there to take the shaver out of the cradle or unplug the cradle from the wall. If the user does leave the shaver pugged in, then it is possible to hear a clicking sound as the shaver keeps trying to recharge every second once the shaver is fully charged. Obviously this is going to shorten the life of the product. The second disappointment is the quality of the stand (not the jet clean system but the small plastic stand). It is very flimsy. If you are travelling with your shaver and you are likely to need to recharge the shaver while you are away, then you have to take the stand with you as there is no direct connection to the shaver other than the stand. Of course, the stand does not fold or fit into the shaver carrying case. These are small matters that with a little more attention to detail Philips could have easily addressed. On balance the quality and quietness of the shave inclines me to rate the product highly. I would have gone for five star if it had not been for the niggly issues. Come on Philips you could do better!

Review: This razor is almost perfect (is there a really perfect shaver, even if you use a blade?). Background: I researched high and low for electric razors as I was tired of paying for blades (they need to be sharp to get close and do not last long). If you use blades, my recommendation is to use at least a 3 blade razor with Kiehl's shave cream - it is, by far, the best shaving cream I have used with a blade (I have not used a safety razor and soap). I receive VERY close shaves with a blade and Kiehl's. I wanted to move from nicks and cuts to easy and and no cuts, even though Kiehl's works well in this area. Enter my history with electric razors. My first was a braun many years ago, which was not close so I did not use electric razors for many year afters. Wanting to experiment again, I went to a cheaper Remington about 8 years ago - the MS-280. It was a lower cost brand, BUT I could get a close shave with this foil shaver. It took more than 10 minutes each time and was DRY only (use remington face saver with this - it works well). Neck is not as close as a blade, but is near blade status, if you spend the time. I had to go over the same areas in different directions (up/down, side to side and diagonal). It did work well but was cheap (on / off button wore off and foils had to be replaced often). It was also very noisy. Now, enter the 3D. It works as it says, wet or dry, which I love. I have used both and will shave wet most of the time after a shower with little risk of cuts. It is quiet and comes with a cleaning machine, which I thought was a gimmick but it works well (I have the 3 mode model, but I assume the next level down shaver, which only has 1 cleaning cycle, does the same cleaning). I can receive as close a shave as a blade except for the neck area. It comes close but I am resigned to the fact that only a blade will remove it as well as it removes it from my face. All electric razors I have used, sans the early Braun (they did not have the brauns they have today so please place it in perspective), have shaved my face well and as close as a blade (but not as fast as a blade). Why I am sticking with the Philips 3D - the shave is very close to a blade. It does not cut me and I can shave more than once in a day if I had to (try that with a blade without tearing your skin up). I can use it wet or dry. Using it wet is very easy and useful. And it is easy to clean. I also reviewed the Panasonic, which I was very close in trying / buying because I did like the Remington foil shaver (3D is rotary). The Braun was out for me since I wanted something I could use in the shower / wet although they receive very good reviews. The charging on this unit could be better. It is confusing to leave it in the cleaner when it will recharge it every time, which I do not think the manufacturers prefer (the instructions are contradictory - why use the cleaning machine when you cannot run the battery level down if you use it?). The unit should have a clean and clean/charge option. This was a miss by Philips. I do have a work around - by a Belkin Conserve power plug. It has a shut-off of 30 mins, 3 or 6 hours. I use the 30 minutes with the Auto / Eco mode (which cuts the drying cycle short) and the 3 hour with the intensive clean. This type of technology, again, should be built into the razor outfit - definitely a design flaw, but it does not impact the shaving. Bottomline: A very good razor that comes very close to a blade. It does what it does well and you do not have to spend time maintaining it. There are some items that could have been designed better for the overall experience, but they do not influence the shaving. This is a nice product for an everyday task that needs to get done (in my world it does).

The time I used it on vacation, it would barely fit in my shaving kit and when I got to my hotel the razor head assembly had fallen out of the body.   339. This razor is an improvement over my past Norelco shavers. Bear in mind that improvements are incremental - it is not like night and day. I switched years ago to a Norelco. I always used a blade before. My problem was that I always tried to get one last shave from the blade before replacing it. I got tired of looking like I needed a transfusion. This is an excellent razor. It is very quiet. Everything is digital, but unobtrusive. I find that I get the best shave by using Gillette Fusion gel and the razor together. It just glides. You can use it in the shower if desired. When I have used it dry, the blades in the head seem to heat and it becomes uncomfortable. Note: The cleaning system for this model offers three options for cleaning. Only one other model of this razor uses a cleaning stand and it has one setting. The difference is how long the unit cleans. I am not sure that it makes a real difference. However, this unit is in the flagship group of Norelco shavers called Senseo Touch 3D.<br /><br />To clean it using the automatic cleaning device, the razor is placed into a holder. It is easy and only goes in one way. On mine, once the cleaning unit is connected to power, the razor is placed with its protective plastic head cover removed into a plastic type of guide that holds the razor. You select the type of cleaning desired by repetitive pushes on a button (there are only three selections). Then, you push the button above the cleaning cycle selector. A small door opens and the razor is lowered into the cleaning solution. After a few seconds of soaking, it starts. It will run on and off for differing amounts of time. Depending on the cycle chosen, it will be lifted out of the solution and held to drain for a minute. Then, it is lowered again into the solution. When it is finished, like a dishwasher, the light changes on the cleaning unit and the razor is lifted from the solution to air dry. Depending on the cleaning cycle chosen this will take from 1 to 2 hours. Then, it is charged. The display will show the amount of charge. It is a digital number which changes orientation depending on how the razor is held. This razor has a number of cool features.<br /><br />Possible drawbacks are: The Cleaning solution is $40 for a 6 pack (and drinking it is not recommended); the razor cannot be run with just its charging cable. It must be charged in either the cleaning stand or on its individual stand which have the electrical contacts to charge the razor. The replacement heads must be replaced as a group about once a year and they are expensive (I think they are about $65 - they are listed on Amazon). My old Norelco Spectra, which is about 10 years old, is still going strong on its original heads.<br /><br />Everything about this razor is quality and it is made in the Netherlands. The icing on the cake is the additional fact that it can be effectively and easily cleaned manually. Norelco has full instructions that are easily understood. Why is this important? Well, while the razor has a two and a half year warranty (when registered), these mechanical cleaning contraptions have been known to last just beyond the warranty. If you think that the replacement heads are expensive, just imagine what a new cleaning base with all of its electronics and motors would cost. So, if the cleaning unit fails, the razor can be just as effectively cleaned manually. My plan is to use the automatic cleaning unit occasionally and otherwise basically clean the razor manually. The reason is that the Fusion gel has to be washed off of the heads before putting the razor into the cleaning unit. So -- it is but another twenty seconds to run hot water over the heads (they life up and tilt open like petals on a flower) to clean them and then set the razor on the stand to manually dry.<br /><br />This is an expensive shaver. I bought it because I happened by accident onto Amazon when they had it reduced for only a few hours by a lot and I still got a $50 discount from Norelco. I have bought from Amazon for 15 years and do so whenever possible because they truly stand behind their products and merchants that they have authorized sellers sell from their site.<br /><br />My opinion is that the head life is maximized when they are not only routinely cleaned, but lubricated. You need to use either this solution or the can of Norelco spray/cleaner, which I also have. I attribute the life of my old Norelco's heads to routine cleaning and lubrication of its heads. Also, on this new Norelco if you take care of the heads you may not have to replace them every year. The razor will warn you to change the heads. Norelco describes how to reset this warning and you have another year. The main warnings are to never use the unit if part of the protective cutting guide over the cutters has broken or is now missing, unless you really want to find what razor burn is like. Also, each cutter takes a set in it own cutting guide. Never, never interchange the cutters into another guide. Norelco cautions you on this. The manual is excellent! I hope that this has not been too long and boring. Steveom Norelco. I have bought from Amazon for 15 years and do so whenever possible because they truly stand behind their products and merchants that they have authorized sellers sell from their site.<br /><br />My opinion is that the head life is maximized when they are not only routinely cleaned, but lubricated.   369. First, I have used this shaver about 4 weeks with shaving cream. I am comparing to my Panasonic ES-LV81 for wet shaving which I have owned just over 2 years. Incidentally, the Panasonic began leaking water into the shaver necessitating my replacement. In comparison, the Panasonic replacement heads/cutter are $65.73. The Norelco requires a different shaving technique than the typical linear foil shavers. Nonetheless, after a few shaves, it was a fairly simple transition. I could shave my face in a minute or two less time with the Norelco. Keys here are a circular motion and on the jaw line using the foils along the jaw line with the Y of the foils straddling the ear lobe to catch those last few whiskers. This shaver is MUCH more comfortable on the neck and Adam's apple area than the Panasonic--which still nicks me frequently in this area. I had no issues with razor burn with the Norelco, even during the initial uses. Other problem areas: right under the nose, it just doesn't reach those hairs very easily; the sideburn area seems to grow in more quickly. I have a rather tough beard. I typically shave daily to avoid the hassles of a longer shave time and missed hairs if I skip days. Nonetheless, this Norelco handled a 2-3 day growth very nicely. With a 5-6 minute shave time (avg 7-8 with the Panasonic) it really is quicker to shave by almost 25%. This unit has a very quiet motor--it is hardly audible! And the shaver is VERY light. Compared to the Buzz saw volume of my Panasonic, I love this feature. The LCD is very attractive and the cleaner is nice, although a bit flimsy. Package includes cleaning solution which should last about a month to 6 weeks. Bottom line: the shaver just does not give me that polished, soft skin after the shave that the Panasonic does. By the end of the day, I feel I need to shave again if I go out with the Norelco (I didn't feel this need as much with the Panasonic). But, it is definitely a decent shave. Considering the ES-LV81 can behad for $279.00 Prime, I would opt for that razor in the same price range. 3 stars based upon the quality of shave, overall feel, cleaner, and looks of device.   423. Update February 2017: I have revised the review for 3 stars from 5 stars. The reasons are: (1) The Jet Clean station that comes with it is simply flawed in its design. It operates fine for a few months, and then the water level sensor becomes dirty or scaled and the unit is unable to properly detect the water/cleaning fluid level, continuously indicating that the fluid reservoir is empty although it is full. Attempts to clean the sensor have inconsistent results. The unit has to be started multiple times until the sensor is eventually able to detect the fluid level and start the cleaning cycle. And eventually the Jet Clean station will cease working altogether, just as my has two weeks ago. Note that my Jet Clean station has been replaced 2 times within the warranty period. The warranty is over and I will absolutely not purchase another one with the same flawed design. The shaver just has to be cleaned manually with similar results. (2) The replacement heads are preposterously expensive. The original heads, RQ12, are no longer manufactured, and the new RQ12+ have been reviewed as below par here at Amazon. It is way too much money invested in electric razors for no reasonable replacement parts... unfortunately common, disposable razors are not an option for me (they do not shave the beard, they remove the skin and the beard), I have not adapted to Braun's shaver system... I might be stuck with Norelco forever. ---- End of Update ---- This one was a replacement for a Norelco 9160XL. Its head holder was worn out, and the razor heads would pop out intermittently during shaving. I had already replaced the head holder once ($25.00) about two years ago, and I was tired of having to do this for a part that should not have to be replaced, in my opinion. I pondered over purchasing a new shaver for quite some time, specially an expensive shaver such as the 1280XL, since the old one was otherwise working fine. I have been using Norelco shavers for 25 years, with a brief 2-3 years interlude of Gillette razors (caused, interestingly, by an incompatibility of electrical plugs when I moved from one country to another two decades ago, and not finding an adapter, forcing me to buy an emergency Gillette razor, taking me 2-3 years to go back to Norelco). I finally asked myself, &#34;how much is worth a good, pleasant shave in the morning, every single day?&#34; I did not think there would be much difference between the 9160XL and this 1280, but I was pleasantly wrong. The shave is smooth, enjoyable, elegantly slides on the face following the natural contours. Only us men know how good of a mood a fine shave can put us into, and this 1280 shaver certainly does it. It is water-proof. I tested it under the shower, it does not fear water. The jet clean system is somewhat bulky. It does, however, perform well and leaves the shaver clean and lubricated. You can of course not purchase the system and clean the shaver under the faucet, but this procedure does waste more water. The system uses the same water with solution for several cleanings. Important: the description at Amazon does not say, but this package *does come* with a charging stand, besides the jet clean system. The charging stand is important if you take the shaver on a trip and do not want to carry the bulky jet system (as the shaver can only be charged either in the jet system, or in the stand).

Shave quality is amazing. (It better be for the amount Norelco is charging for the replacement heads!) Speaking of those, I have not seen a price any cheaper than what they sell for here on Amazon so you may want to buy a pack or two when you see the price drop on Amazon that way you don't have to buy them from a physical store where you'll easily pay $5-$10 more for the same replacement heads.<br /><br />6. The shaving surface rotates nicely to match your facial curves. Compared to previous models, Norelco has made huge strides in improvement in this area. Shaving is comfortable and close.<br /><br />6. Compared to my previous razor, this one is quieter, in fact, it is so quiet that you can actually hear someone talking outside of the bathroom which is nice as I always seem to get interrupted with questions while I'm trying to shave! At least now I can hear people. Also good for when you need to shave at night and not make a ton of noise.<br /><br />7. Cleaning kit: As I mentioned above, I do use the cleaning kit with mine because it came with one when I purchased it, however, I really don't think you need it as simply running the blades under warm water removes most of the hair particles. Once you've done that, you can open up the head cover and get an even deeper clean. As long as you do this maybe once a week or so, you shouldn't need the cleaning kit. This could save you quite a bit of money if you find one somewhere that's sold by itself without the cleaning kit.<br /><br />*** CONCLUSION ***<br /><br />I honestly think you'll get quite a few years out of this razor before needing to purchase something new. I'll update this review if I notice any problems with it as it gets older and more use. For right now, after 6-months of use, it's working as well as the day I bought it and I stillhaven't needed to change the heads, although I probably will sometime this month.
